    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-985</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1748-3387</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgw5j--xlnopQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201209689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity and Rate Capability of Amorphous Phosphorus for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew. Peter; Kupsta, Martin; Zahiri, Beniamin; Kohandehghan, Alireza; Lotfabad, Elmira Memarzadeh; Li, Zhi; Luber, Erik J.; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we provide the first report on several compns. of ternary Sn-Ge-Sb thin film alloys for application as sodium ion battery (aka NIB, NaB or SIB) anodes, employing Sn50Ge50, Sb50Ge50, and pure Sn, Ge, Sb as baselines.  Sn33Ge33Sb33, Sn50Ge25Sb25, Sn60Ge20Sb20, and Sn50Ge50 all demonstrate promising electrochem. behavior, with Sn50Ge25Sb25 being the best overall.  This alloy has an initial reversible specific capacity of 833 mAhg-1 (at 85 mAg-1) and 662 mAhg-1 after 50 charge-discharge cycles.  Sn50Ge25Sb25 also shows excellent rate capability, displaying a stable capacity of 381 mAhg-1 at a c.d. of 8500 mAg-1 (∼10C).  A survey of published literature indicates that 833 mAhg-1 is among the highest reversible capacities reported for a Sn-based NIB anode, while 381 mAhg-1 represents the optimum fast charge value.  HRTEM shows that Sn50Ge25Sb25 is a composite of 10-15 nm Sn and Sn-alloyed Ge nanocrystallites that are densely dispersed within an amorphous matrix.  Comparing the microstructures of alloys where the capacity significantly exceeds the rule of mixts. prediction to those where it does not leads us to hypothesize that this new phenomenon originates from the Ge(Sn) that is able to sodiate beyond the 1:1 Na:Ge ratio reported for the pure element.  Combined TOF-SIMS, EELS TEM, and FIB anal. demonstrates substantial Na segregation within the film near the current collector interface that is present as early as the second discharge, followed by cycling-induced delamination from the current collector.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVb3oOuj1ecbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj2xC2dDb1y6w"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun Sb/C Fibers for a Stable and Fast Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Han, Xiaogang; Xu, Yunhua; Liu, Yihang; Zheng, Shiyou; Xu, Kang; Hu, Liangbing; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6378-6386</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a top alternative to Li-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of Na-bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  However, the development of anode materials for SIBs to date was mainly limited to carbonaceous materials with minimal research devoted to high capacity alloy-based materials.  An Sb/C electrode with ∼30 nm Sb nanoparticles (NPs) uniformly encapsulated in interconnecting 1-dimensional (1D) 400 nm C fibers (denoted as SbNP@C) was fabricated using a simple and scalable electrospinning method.  This binder-free, current collector-free SbNP@C electrode demonstrated high capacity and stable long-term cycling performance at various current densities.  The SbNP@C electrode showed an initial total capacity of 422 mA-h/gelectrode and retained 350 mA-h/gelectrode after 300 deep charge-discharge cycles under 100 mA/gSb.  Also, because of the efficient 1-dimensional Na-ion transport pathway and the highly conductive network of SbNP@C, the electrode preserved high overall capacities even when cycled at high currents, extending its usability to high power applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCf3y1wC4rXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj2xC2dDb1y6w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWht7nJ&amp;md5=382586ead9328ea5a3721bf05276e705</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00114"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitlin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin and Tin Compounds for Sodium Ion Battery Anodes: Phase Transformations and Performance</span>. <i>Acc. Chem. Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>48</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1657</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1665</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00114</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D48%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D1657-1665%26journal%3DAcc.%2BChem.%2BRes.%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BDing%26author%3DD.%2BMitlin%26title%3DTin%2Band%2BTin%2BCompounds%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%2BAnodes%253A%2BPhase%2BTransformations%2Band%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.accounts.5b00114&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b05134&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.accounts.5b00114&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin and Tin Compounds for Sodium Ion Battery Anodes: Phase Transformations and Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhi; Ding, Jia; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">48</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1657-1665</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium ion batteries (NIB, NAB, SIB) are attracting interest as a potentially lower cost alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIB), with readily available and geog. democratic reserves of the metal.  Tin is one of most promising SIB anode materials, which alloys with up to 3.75 Na, leading to a charge storage capacity of 847 mAh g-1.  In this Account, we outline the state-of-the-art understanding regarding the sodiation-induced phase transformations and the assocd. performance in a range of Sn-based systems, treating metallic Sn and its alloys, tin oxide (SnO2), tin sulfide (SnS2/SnS), and tin phosphide (Sn4P3).  We first detail what is known about the sodiation sequence in metallic Sn, highlighting the most recent insight into the reactions prior to the terminal equil. Na15Sn4 intermetallic.  We explain why researchers argue that the equil. (phase diagram) series of phase transitions does not occur in this system, and rather why sodiation/desodiation proceeds through a series of metastable cryst. and amorphous structures.  We also outline the recent modeling-based insight regarding how this phase transition profoundly influences the mech. properties of the alloy, progressively changing the bonding and the near neighbor arrangement from "Sn-like" to "Na-like" in the process.  We then go on to discuss the sodiation reactions in SnO2.  We argue that while a substantial amt. of exptl. work already exists where the focus is on synthesis and testing of tin oxide-based nanocomposites, the exact sodiation sequence is just beginning to be understood.  Unlike in Sn and Sn alloys, where capacities near the theor. are reached at least early during cycling, SnO2 never quite achieves anything close to the 1398 mAh g-1 that would be possible with a combination of fully reversible conversion and alloying reactions.  We highlight recent work demonstrating that contrary to general expectations, it is the Sn to Na15Sn4 alloying reaction that is incomplete and hence limits the capacity of the electrode.  We also describe how the oxide conversion reaction goes through an intermediate SnO phase, and how its reversibility in a half-cell is highly dependent on the terminal anodic voltage.  We then present what is known about sodiation of tin sulfide and of tin phosphide phases, including emerging microstructural evidence that may explain why both the sulfides and the phosphides are unable to achieve their highly promising theor. capacities under conventional electrode testing conditions.  Finally, we provide a broad comparison of the capacity (cycling and rate) performance for a range of Sn based anode materials, and show that there may be indeed an optimum microstructural architecture.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGraHWeuL6zqAbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgizp46H4SaWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtVakurzM&amp;md5=7305836f3a3bbf9d5e81e811cd8ab069</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402943"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for Na-ion batteries, ultra-small Sn nanoparticles (≈8 nm) homogeneously embedded in spherical C network (denoted as 8-Sn@C) is prepd. using an aerosol spray pyrolysis method.  Instrumental analyses show that 8-Sn@C nanocomposite with 46% Sn and a BET surface area of 150.43 m2 g-1 delivers an initial reversible capacity of ≈493.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 200 mA g-1, a high-rate capacity of 349 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1, and a stable capacity of ≈415 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1000 mA g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 8-Sn@C is owing to the synergetic effects between the well-dispersed ultra-small Sn nanoparticles and the conductive C network.  This unique structure of very-fine Sn nanoparticles embedded in the porous C network can effectively suppress the vol. fluctuation and particle aggregation of Sn during prolonged sodiation/desodiation process, thus solving the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact and low use rate facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIJZ-8q45agLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgizp46H4SaWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVKksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=bf146b366c93613b170938edd33ec0fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta13592f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, Y.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafine SnO2 nanoparticle loading onto reduced graphene oxide as anodes for sodium-ion batteries with superior rate and cycling performances</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yun-Xiao; Lim, Young-Geun; Park, Min-Sik; Chou, Shu-Lei; Kim, Jung Ho; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue; Kim, Young-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

It has been successfully applied as an anode material in sodium-ion batteries.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-capacity antimony sulphide nanoparticle-decorated graphene composite as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu Denis Y W; Prikhodchenko Petr V; Mason Chad W; Batabyal Sudip K; Gun Jenny; Sladkevich Sergey; Medvedev Alexander G; Lev Ovadia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes are the main bottlenecks to future developments.  Here we report a uniform coating of antimony sulphide (stibnite) on graphene, fabricated by a solution-based synthesis technique, as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It gives a high capacity of 730 mAh g(-1) at 50 mA g(-1), an excellent rate capability up to 6C and a good cycle performance.  The promising performance is attributed to fast sodium ion diffusion from the small nanoparticles, and good electrical transport from the intimate contact between the active material and graphene, which also provides a template for anchoring the nanoparticles.  We also demonstrate a battery with the stibnite-graphene composite that is free from sodium metal, having energy density up to 80 Wh kg(-1).                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1309-1316</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwLzI_bTYOsw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms9689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres for superior sodium-iron sulfide batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yun-Xiao; Yang, Jianping; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua Kun; Zhang, Wei-xian; Zhao, Dongyuan; Dou, Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8689</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.  The proven conversion reaction between sodium and iron sulfide results in high capacity but severe vol. changes.  Nanostructural design, including of nanosized iron sulfide yolks (∼170 nm) with porous carbon shells (∼30 nm) and extra void space (∼20 nm) in between, has been used to achieve excellent cycling performance without sacrificing capacity.  This sustainable sodium-iron sulfide battery is a promising candidate for stationary energy storage.  Furthermore, this spatially confined sulfuration strategy offers a general method for other yolk-shell metal sulfide-carbon composites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsA2QzawgLO7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwLzI_bTYOsw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslCnt7vP&amp;md5=6002aabf08f2ca14f26ecb4cd8008b28</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201404078"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1393</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1403</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Xiuqiang; Ao, Zhimin; Su, Dawei; Zhang, Jinqiang; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1393-1403</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene has been widely used as conformal nanobuilding blocks to improve the electrochem. performance of layered metal sulfides (MoS2, WS2, SnS, and SnS2) as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  However, it still lacks in-depth understanding of the synergistic effect between these layered sulfides and graphene, which contributes to the enhanced electroactivity for sodium-ion batteries.  Here, MoS2/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanocomposites with intimate two-dimensional heterointerfaces are prepd. by a facile one-pot hydrothermal method.  The heterointerfacial area can be effectively tuned by changing the ratio of MoS2 to RGO.  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries, the synergistic effect contributing to the enhanced reversible capacity of MoS2/RGO nanocomposites is closely related with the heterointerfacial area.  The computational results demonstrate that Na prefers to be adsorbed on MoS2 in the MoS2/RGO heterostructure rather than intercalate into the MoS2/RGO heterointerface.  Interestingly, the MoS2/RGO heterointerfaces can significantly increase the electronic cond. of MoS2, store more Na ions, while maintaining the high diffusion mobility of Na atoms on MoS2 surface and high electron transfer efficiency from Na to MoS2.  It is expected that the efforts to establish the correlation between the two-dimensional heterointerface and the electrochem. sodium-ion storage performance offer fundamental understanding for the rational design of layered metal sulfides/graphene composites as high-performance electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpB50PmkRDAvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lit2ZcCRR2Rqg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Nanospheres Constructed by Ultrathin MoS2 Nanosheets Braced on Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Polyhedra for Efficient Lithium and Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tu, Fengzhang; Han, Yu; Du, Yichen; Ge, Xufang; Weng, Wangsuo; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 has attracted a lot of attention for electrochem. energy storage.  Herein, unusual hierarchical composite nanospheres are designed and fabricated by cultivating a MoS2 sheet-like nanostructure on nitrogen-doped carbon polyhedra (designated as CP@MoS2 nanospheres).  The nitrogen-doped carbon polyhedra are able to significantly boost the elec. cond. of the hybrid architecture and largely mitigate the agglomeration of the MoS2 nanostructure.  The sheet-like MoS2 nanostructure can render a great deal of storage sites toward lithium and sodium.  When measured as a neg. electrode for Li storage, these CP@MoS2 nanospheres manifest a large charge capacity of approx. 549 mAh g-1, a superior cycle life of 900 cycles, and excellent rate property.  Furthermore, they also demonstrate improved electrochem. activity for Na+ ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp4WEgY_CyuwbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lit2ZcCRR2Rqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisFyltbnK&amp;md5=e603fda2c8905a04a0eea1c12cc3c4b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2015.06.064"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ko, Y.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Co9S8-carbon composite as anode materials with improved Na-storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ko, You Na; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The synthesis and electrochem. performance of a composite of Co9S8 nanoparticles and amorphous carbon is studied as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The Co9S8-carbon composite powder was fabricated through a one-pot spray pyrolysis process using thiourea and polyvinylpyrrolidone as sulfur and carbon sources, resp.  The Co9S8 nanoparticles are entirely covered by an amorphous carbon layer.  The initial discharge and charge capacities of the Co9S8-carbon composite powder were 689 and 475 mA h g-1, resp., at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.  The Co9S8-carbon composite powders exhibited a stable cyclability with a reversible capacity of 404 mA h g-1 for the 50th cycle and a superior rate capability compared with bare Co1-xS powder.  The improvement of Na-storage performance could be attributed to the small size and entanglement of the Co9S8 nanoparticles within the carbon matrix.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpKmwBER2XPJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lit2ZcCRR2Rqg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fiber-in-Tube Design of Co9S8-Carbon/Co9S8: Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xiaoyan; Li, Kaikai; Zhu, Sicong; Fan, Ke; Lyu, Linlong; Yao, Haimin; Li, Yiyang; Hu, Jinlian; Huang, Haitao; Mai, Yiu-Wing; Goodenough, John B.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion battery is a promising battery technol. owing to its low price and high abundance of sodium.  However, the sluggish kinetics of sodium ion makes it hard to achieve high-rate performance, therefore impairing the power d.  A fiber-in-tube Co9S8-carbon(C)/Co9S8 is designed with fast sodiation kinetics.  The exptl. and simulation anal. show that the dominating capacitance mechanism for the high Na-ion storage performance is due to abundant grain boundaries, three exposed layer interfaces, and carbon wiring in the design.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MOF-Derived Hollow Co9S8 Nanoparticles Embedded in Graphitic Carbon Nanocages with Superior Li-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Jun; Wu, Chao; Xiao, Dongdong; Kopold, Peter; Gu, Lin; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

Owing to the good mech. flexibility and pronounced structure stability of carbon nanocages-encapsulated Co9S8, the as-obtained HCSP⊂GCC exhibit superior Li-ion storage.  Working in the voltage of 1.0-3.0 V, they display a very high energy d. (707 Wh kg-1), superior rate capability (reversible capabilities of 536, 489, 438, 393, 345, and 278 mA h g-1 at 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10C, resp.), and stable cycling performance (≈26% capacity loss after long 150 cycles at 1C with a capacity retention of 365 mA h g-1).                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Integrated Hierarchical Cobalt Sulfide/Nickel Selenide Hybrid Nanosheets as an Efficient Three-dimensional Electrode for Electrochemical and Photoelectrochemical Water Splitting</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Yang; Qiu, Ming; Nam, Gyutae; Kim, Min Gyu; Zhang, Tao; Liu, Kejun; Zhuang, Xiaodong; Cho, Jaephil; Yuan, Chris; Feng, Xinliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4202-4209</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing highly active electrocatalysts for photoelectrochem. water splitting is crit. to bring solar/elec.-to-hydrogen energy conversion processes into reality.  Herein, we report a three-dimensional (3D) hybrid electrocatalyst that is constructed through in situ anchoring of Co9S8 nanosheets onto the surface of Ni3Se2 nanosheets vertically aligned on an electrochem. exfoliated graphene foil.  Benefiting from the synergistic effects between Ni3Se2 and Co9S8, the highly conductive graphene support, and large surface area, the novel 3D hybrid electrode delivers superior electrocatalytic activity toward water redn. in alk. media, featuring overpotentials of -0.17 and -0.23 V to achieve current densities of 20 and 50 mA cm-2, resp., demonstrating an electrocatalytic performance on the top of the Ni3Se2- and Co9S8-based electrocatalysts as reported in literature.  Exptl. investigations and theor. calcns. confirm that the remarkable activity of the obtained material results from the unique 3D hierarchical architecture and interface reconstruction between Ni3Se2 and Co9S8 through Ni-S bonding, which leads to charge redistribution and thus lowers the energy barrier of hydrogen desorption in the water splitting process.  Further integration of the 3D hybrid electrode with a macroporous silicon photocathode enables highly active and sustainable sunlight-driven water splitting in both basic media and real river water.  The overall water splitting with 10 mA cm-2 at a low voltage of 1.62 V is achieved using our hybrid as both anode and cathode catalysts, which surpasses that of the Ir/C-Pt/C couple (1.60 V) for sufficiently high overpotentials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvsRwgVsIZnbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrdlW5p4ZCCA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Armored Co9S8 Nanoparticles as All-pH Efficient and Durable H2-Evolving Electrocatalysts</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Liang-Liang; Li, Guo-Dong; Liu, Yipu; Wu, Yuanyuan; Chen, Hui; Wang, Yun; Zou, Yong-Cun; Wang, Dejun; Zou, Xiaoxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-988</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Splitting H2O to produce H requires the development of nonnoble-metal catalysts that are able to make this reaction feasible and energy efficient.  Herein, Co pentlandite (Co9S8) nanoparticles can serve as an electrochem. active, noble-metal-free material toward H evolution reaction, and they work stably in neutral soln. (pH 7) but not in acidic (pH 0) and basic (pH 14) media.  The authors, therefore, further present a C-armoring strategy to increase the durability and activity of Co9S8 over a wider pH range.  In particular, C-armored Co9S8 nanoparticles (Co9S8@C) are prepd. by direct thermal treatment of a mixt. of Co nitrate and trithiocyanuric acid at 700° in N2 atmosphere.  Trithiocyanuric acid functions as both S and C sources in the reaction system.  The resulting Co9S8@C material operates well with high activity over a broad pH range, from pH 0 to 14, and gives nearly 100% faradaic yield during H evolution reaction under acidic (pH 0), neutral (pH 7), and basic (pH 14) media.  This is the 1st time that a transition-metal chalcogenide material has all-pH efficient and durable electrocatalytic activity.  Identifying Co9S8 as the catalytically active phase and developing C-armoring as the improvement strategy are anticipated to give a fresh impetus to rational design of high-performance noble-metal-free H2O splitting catalysts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo8WDE7ehfcjrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrdlW5p4ZCCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFehtr7M&amp;md5=aed13c4ec4b7076cfe17fb237cc6b9af</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1039/c5ta06158j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphene/Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> Nanocomposite Paper as A Binder-Free and Free-Standing Anode for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem.                 10.1039/c5ta06158j</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D23677-23683%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DS.%2BLu%26author%3DY.%2BChen%26author%3DL.%2BHan%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DX.%2BWu%26author%3DW.%2BQin%26title%3DGraphene%252FCo9S8%2BNanocomposite%2BPaper%2Bas%2BA%2BBinder-Free%2Band%2BFree-Standing%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc5ta06158j&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b05134&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc5ta06158j&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene/Co9S8 nanocomposite paper as a binder-free and free-standing anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Huanhuan; Lu, Songtao; Chen, Yan; Han, Lu; Zhou, Jia; Wu, Xiaohong; Qin, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23677-23683</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible lithium ion batteries with high energy d. have recently received tremendous interest due to their potential applications in flexible electronic devices.  Herein, we report a simple high energy ball-milling technique together with vacuum filtration to fabricate a highly flexible, conductive, robust and free-standing RGO/Co9S8 nanocomposite paper with high cond. (121 S cm-1), tensile strength (50.4 MPa) and Young's modulus (3.5 GPa) which can be directly used as a free-standing anode for flexible LIBs without binders, conducting agents and metallic current collectors.  The free-standing RGO/Co9S8 anode with a high mass active material loading of 66.7 wt% Co9S8 can deliver a high specific capacity of 1415 mA h gCo9S8-1 (944 mA h gelectrode-1) and maintain 573 mA h gCo9S8-1 (382.2 mA h gelectrode-1) after 500 cycles at a c.d. of 1C (1C = 545 mA g-1).  More importantly, the rate capability was improved by introducing RGO.  The RGO/Co9S8 anode exhibited impressive capacities of 1096.70 mA h gCo9S8-1 with a capacity recuperation ability of 69.4% as the current returned to 0.1C.  These results demonstrate that the well designed nanocomposite is of great potential as an anode for flexible LIBs.  As far as we know, such improved electrochem. performance can be attributed to the nanosized Co9S8 particles with a diam. of ∼25 nm homogeneously dispersed on the surface of high conductive graphene sheets that can be obtained owing to the milling impact stress, which enhances surface electrochem. reactivity and shortens the transport length of lithium ions and electrons.  What's more, the large sp. surface area of the graphene sheet enables the uniform distribution of Co9S8 and offers better ability to accommodate vol. expansion/shrinkage of Co9S8 during repeated charge/discharge cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqO4sDLjWeCD7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrdlW5p4ZCCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1Kksb3E&amp;md5=4bba57a2ad55ddf6cb665ddc02064dff</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/jz200223x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Worsley, M.

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Surface Area, sp2-Cross-Linked Three-Dimensional Graphene Monoliths</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Worsley, Marcus A.; Olson, Tammy Y.; Lee, Jonathan R. I.; Willey, Trevor M.; Nielsen, Michael H.; Roberts, Sarah K.; Pauzauskie, Peter J.; Biener, Juergen; Satcher, Joe H.; Baumann, Theodore F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing three-dimensional (3D) graphene assemblies with properties similar to those individual graphene sheets is a promising strategy for graphene-based electrodes.  Typically, the synthesis of 3D graphene assemblies relies on van der Waals forces for holding the graphene sheets together, resulting in bulk properties that do not reflect those reported for individual graphene sheets.  Here, we report the use of sol-gel chem. to introduce chem. bonding between the graphene sheets and control the bulk properties of graphene-based aerogels.  Adjusting synthetic parameters allows a wide range of control over surface area, pore vol., and pore size, as well as the nature of the chem. cross-links (sp2 vs sp3).  The bulk properties of the graphene-based aerogels represent a significant step toward realizing the properties of individual graphene sheets in a 3D assembly with surface areas approaching the theor. value of an individual sheet.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqdvNvNg6NYnbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li3eo4xLi9Elw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXkt1Wnsrk%253D&amp;md5=f8bf6c431ea5c5da873f6d6b9225f79f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1039/c6ta09580a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mesoporous Nitrogen, Sulfur Co-Doped Carbon Dots/CoS Hybrid as An Efficient Electrocatalyst for Hydrogen Evolution</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous nitrogen, sulfur co-doped carbon dots/CoS hybrid as an efficient electrocatalyst for hydrogen evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Liping; Wu, Xiuqin; Guo, Sijie; Han, Mumei; Zhou, Yunjie; Sun, Yue; Huang, Hui; Liu, Yang; Kang, Zhenhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hydrogen is an ideal energy carrier for renewable energy, but a high overpotential is required to achieve reasonable H2 evolution, which makes the design of highly active electrocatalysts for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) urgent.  Here, a nitrogen, sulfur co-doped carbon dots (NSCDs)/CoS hybrid with a three-dimensional mesoporous sponge-like nanostructure, fabricated via heat-treatment, which as electrocatalyst exhibits the desired electrocatalytic activity for electrochem. HER is reported.  A series of NSCDs/CoS hybrids with different contents of NSCDs were prepd. by adjusting the concn. of NSCDs, of which the NSCDs/CoS hybrid with 20 mg L-1 NSCDs exhibits the best electrocatalytic activity towards HER with an onset potential of 0.095 V, an overpotential at 10 mA cm-2 of 165 mV, a small Tafel slope of 56 mV per decade, and a good stability in 0.5 M H2SO4.  The excellent electrocatalytic activity of NSCDs/CoS for HER is attributed to synergetic effects of NSCDs and CoS, in which the NSCDs could protect the CoS from dissoln./agglomeration under acidic conditions, and the increased surface area of the NSCDs/CoS hybrid and the high charge transfer efficiency between NSCDs and CoS via Co-S-C bonding enhanced the HER performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp51z5iGqY0SrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li3eo4xLi9Elw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFOgsb7N&amp;md5=7d5f9448e634bd9c113dc22049f0f4cb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.03.183"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of self-assembled cobalt sulphide coated carbon nanotube and its superior electrochemical performance as anodes for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Zhi Xiang; Wang, Ye; Wong, Jen It; Shi, Wen Hui; Yang, Hui Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Co sulfide/functionalized C nanotube (CoS2/fCNT) nanocomposites were synthesized via solvothermal method followed by annealing sulfidation.  The nanocomposites were composed of fine nanoparticles (2-10 nm) coated along the surfaces of fCNT as well as nanoclusters (30-60 nm) formed by the nanoparticles which intertwined with the fCNT network.  The as-synthesized CoS2/fCNT nanocomposites exhibited excellent electrochem. performance as an anode material in Li-ion batteries (LIBs), such as superior specific capacity, enhanced rate capability, outstanding cycling stability and near 100% Coulombic efficiency.  CoS2/fCNT hybrid nanocomposite electrodes were able to deliver high reversible capacities of 783.4 mAh g-1 and 337.8 mAh g-1 at the current densities of 50 and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  Also, the electrode sustained an impressive capacity retention of 84.1% after unprecedented 1000 discharge-charge cycles at a high c.d. of 1000 mAh g-1 The ultra-long cycle stability is much higher than all other reported Co sulfide anodes so far.  The excellent electrochem. performance of CoS2/fCNT nanocomposite is attributed to the synergistic effects of CoS2 and fCNT.  The outstanding stability of the CoS2/fCNT nanocomposites makes it a highly promising anode material to instead of the conventional graphite for future generation LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoH9acc8rEdoLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li3eo4xLi9Elw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXlsVOmuro%253D&amp;md5=0665ac516763b601b6cfe5a9078fee5d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1039/c6ta10272g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A facile sol-gel route to prepare functional graphene nanosheets anchored with homogeneous cobalt sulfide nanoparticles as superb sodium-ion anodes</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A facile sol-gel route to prepare functional graphene nanosheets anchored with homogeneous cobalt sulfide nanoparticles as superb sodium-ion anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Tingting; Ma, Yifan; Guo, Qiubo; Yang, Mei; Xia, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid metal sulfides with a graphene matrix is an efficient design to buffer the vol. expansion and fragmentation of vulnerable metal sulfides.  However, the prepn. of graphene oxide is commonly the first step to obtain metal sulfide/graphene composites.  In this work, the prepn. is integrated of functional graphene nanosheets (FGNs) and the growth of electrochem. active cobalt sulfide (Co1-xS) nanoparticles into the same synthesis procedure by a facile sol-gel method to prep. Co1-xS/FGN nanocomposites.  The FGNs not only function as a powerful support for the loading of electrochem. active Co1-xS nanoparticles, which can effectively prevent the re-stacking of the FGNs in turn, but also furnish addnl. electrochem. active sites for sodium ion storage.                 10.1021/acsnano.7b07132</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D12658-12667%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DQ.%2BGuo%26author%3DY.%2BMa%26author%3DT.%2BChen%26author%3DQ.%2BXia%26author%3DM.%2BYang%26author%3DH.%2BXia%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26title%3DCobalt%2BSulfide%2BQuantum%2BDot%2BEmbedded%2BN%252FS-Doped%2BCarbon%2BNanosheets%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BReversibility%2Band%2BRate%2BCapability%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.7b07132&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b05134&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b07132&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt Sulfide Quantum Dot Embedded N/S-Doped Carbon Nanosheets with Superior Reversibility and Rate Capability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Qiubo; Ma, Yifan; Chen, Tingting; Xia, Qiuying; Yang, Mei; Xia, Hui; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12658-12667</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal sulfides are promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries due to their large specific capacities.  The practical applications of metal sulfides in sodium-ion batteries, however, are still limited due to their large vol. expansion, poor cycling stability, and sluggish electrode kinetics.  In this work, a two-dimensional heterostructure of CoSx (CoS and Co9S8) quantum dots embedded N/S-doped carbon nanosheets (CoSx@NSC) is prepd. by a sol-gel method.  The CoSx quantum dots are in situ formed within ultrafine carbon nanosheets without further sulfidation, thus resulting in ultrafine CoSx particle size and embedded heterostructure.  Meanwhile, enriched N and S codoping in the carbon nanosheets greatly enhances the elec. cond. for the conductive matrix and creates more active sites for sodium storage.  As a result, the hybrid CoSx@NSC electrode shows excellent rate capability (600 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 and 500 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and outstanding cycling stability (87% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1), making it promising as an anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries.  A CoSx@NSC//Na0.44MnO2 full cell is demonstrated, and it can deliver a specific capacity of 414 mAh g-1 (based on the mass of CoSx@NSC) at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9OkEmDbmxnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgn6W3CkzU-iw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVaku7bJ&amp;md5=366aa605bfae1bf5095b737a7b5b3c40</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1039/c6cs00776g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-Ion Batteries: Present and Future</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgn6W3CkzU-iw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Array of nanosheets render ultrafast and high-capacity Na-ion storage by tunable pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Zhu, Changrong; Yang, Peihua; Xia, Xinhui; Liu, Jilei; Wang, Jin; Fan, Xiaofeng; Savilov, Serguei V.; Lin, Jianyi; Fan, Hong Jin; Shen, Ze Xiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a potentially low-cost and safe alternative to the prevailing lithium-ion battery technol.  However, it is a great challenge to achieve fast charging and high power d. for most sodium-ion electrodes because of the sluggish sodiation kinetics.  Here we demonstrate a high-capacity and high-rate sodium-ion anode based on ultrathin layered tin(II) sulfide nanostructures, in which a maximized extrinsic pseudocapacitance contribution is identified and verified by kinetics anal.  The graphene foam supported tin(II) sulfide nanoarray anode delivers a high reversible capacity of ∼1,100 mAh g-1 at 30 mA g-1 and ∼420 mAh g-1 at 30 A g-1, which even outperforms its lithium-ion storage performance.  The surface-dominated redox reaction rendered by our tailored ultrathin tin(II) sulfide nanostructures may also work in other layered materials for high-performance sodium-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVSw-KQ43s-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgC1AReUQP3g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFSqtLbO&amp;md5=3f7ab452279e7159794a832183e58387</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1039/c5ta00621j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> Porous Nanosheets Embedded in Graphene Sheets as High-Performance Anode Materials for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J.                 10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D32%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D12593-12602%26journal%3DLangmuir%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.%2BDong%26author%3DQ.%2BFan%26author%3DQ.%2BKuang%26title%3DSynthesis%2Bof%2Bthe%2BCarbon-Coated%2BNanoparticle%2BCo9S8%2Band%2BIts%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bas%2BAn%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.langmuir.6b02870&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b05134&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.6b02870&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co9S8 and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xudong; Liu, Huatao; Zhao, Yanming; Dong, Youzhong; Fan, Qinghua; Kuang, Quan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Langmuir</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12593-12602</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">LANGD5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0743-7463</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A Co9S8/C nanocomposite is prepd. using a solid-state reaction followed by a facile mech. ball-milling treatment, with sucrose as the carbon source.  The phases, morphologies, and detailed structures of the Co9S8/C nanocomposite are well-characterized using X-ray diffraction (XRD), XPS, and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy.  When evaluated as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, the Co9S8/C nanocomposite electrode displays a reversible capacity of ∼567 mA h g-1 in the initial cycle and maintains a reversible capacity of ∼320 mA h g-1 after 30 cycles, indicating a larger capacity and a stable cycling performance.  For comparison, the electrochem. performances of Co9S8 and Co9S8/C samples synthesized using the solid-state reaction are also displayed.  The ex situ XRD and transmission electron microscopy tests demonstrate that Co9S8 undergoes a conversion-type sodium storage mechanism.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpYN4dlHrKKYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMmnlMA2I0YA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslGhurbE&amp;md5=f8a6b16adfd9eef5aa00ea49f961d918</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/c6ta01497f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> @Polyaniline Nanotubes as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5505</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5516</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c6ta01497f</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D5505-5516%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DQ.%2BZhou%26author%3DL.%2BLiu%26author%3DZ.%2BHuang%26author%3DL.%2BYi%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DG.%2BCao%26title%3DCo3S4%2B%2540Polyaniline%2BNanotubes%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc6ta01497f&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b05134&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc6ta01497f&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Co3S4@polyaniline nanotubes as high-performance anode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Qian; Liu, Li; Huang, Zhifeng; Yi, Lingguang; Wang, Xianyou; Cao, Guozhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5505-5516</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, by employing Co3S4 nanotubes prepd. by a facile self-template hydrothermal route based on the Kirkendall effect, Co3S4@polyaniline (Co3S4@PANI) nanotubes, in which polyaniline is uniformly coated on both exterior and inner surfaces of Co3S4 nanotubes, were fabricated through in situ oxidative polymn.  Benefiting from the highly conductive and mech. robust polyaniline shell, the cond. and stability of the composite were significantly improved.  As a result, Co3S4@PANI nanotubes demonstrate much better electrochem. performance than bare Co3S4 nanotubes as sodium ion battery anode materials, with a high capacity of 252.5 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at the c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  In contrast, although a specific capacity of the bare Co3S4 nanotubes in the first cycle achieved was 815.3 mA h g-1, it rapidly decayed to 192.9 mA h g-1 at the 20th cycle and further reduced to 58.2 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles.  Furthermore, Co3S4@PANI nanotubes showed a high discharge capacity of 170.1 mA h g-1 after 400 cycles with a large c.d. of 4000 mA g-1.  The excellent electrochem. properties of Co3S4@PANI nanotubes were ascribed to the combination of Co3S4 and PANI and the stability of the composite structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGriN1XIFX_muLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMmnlMA2I0YA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XktFegtr8%253D&amp;md5=ccd7cce3e7226f8a324b56da388452e9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201600964"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kopold, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maier, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Peapod-Like Carbon-Encapsulated Cobalt Chalcogenide Nanowires as Cycle-Stable and High-Rate Materials for Sodium-Ion Anodes</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/adma.201600964</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D7276-7283%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26author%3DP.%2BKopold%26author%3DP.%2BA.%2Bvan%2BAken%26author%3DJ.%2BMaier%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26title%3DPeapod-Like%2BCarbon-Encapsulated%2BCobalt%2BChalcogenide%2BNanowires%2Bas%2BCycle-Stable%2Band%2BHigh-Rate%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201600964&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b05134&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201600964&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Peapod-Like Carbon-Encapsulated Cobalt Chalcogenide Nanowires as Cycle-Stable and High-Rate Materials for Sodium-Ion Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Chao; Jiang, Yu; Kopold, Peter; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7276-7283</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This article describes about the peapod-like carbon-encapsulated cobalt chalcogenide nanowires as cycle-stable and high-rate materials for sodium-ion anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3xW-zU9JmJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMmnlMA2I0YA"> &gt;&gt;
